citraks__: Penyadapan telepon seluler tanpa izin di Indonesia, termasuk melalui aplikasi seperti WhatsApp (WA), melanggar Undang-Undang Informasi dan Transaksi Elektronik (UU ITE). Pasal yang relevan adalah Pasal 31 ayat (1) dan Pasal 46 ayat (1) UU ITE, yang mengatur tentang larangan intersepsi (penyadapan) informasi elektronik tanpa hak dan melawan hukum. Pelaku penyadapan ilegal dapat dikenai sanksi pidana penjara dan denda. 
Penjelasan Lebih Lanjut:
UU ITE dan Penyadapan:
UU ITE mengatur tentang informasi dan transaksi elektronik, termasuk larangan penyadapan. 
Pasal 31 ayat (1) UU ITE:
Melarang setiap orang dengan sengaja dan tanpa hak atau melawan hukum melakukan penyadapan atas informasi elektronik dan/atau dokumen elektronik dalam suatu komputer dan/atau sistem elektronik tertentu milik orang lain. 
Pasal 46 ayat (1) UU ITE:
Mengatur sanksi pidana bagi mereka yang melanggar ketentuan Pasal 30 UU ITE, termasuk penyadapan. 
Sanksi:
Pelanggaran Pasal 30 ayat (1) UU ITE (mengakses tanpa hak atau melawan hukum) dapat dikenai pidana penjara paling lama 6 tahun dan/atau denda paling banyak Rp600 juta. 
Penyadapan oleh Pihak Berwenang:
Penyadapan oleh penegak hukum dalam rangka penegakan hukum diatur dalam undang-undang dan tidak termasuk dalam larangan penyadapan ilegal. 
Penyadapan dalam Hubungan Khusus:
Meskipun ada hubungan khusus seperti suami istri, penyadapan oleh salah satu pihak tanpa izin tetap dianggap melanggar privasi dan dapat dikenai sanksi hukum, meskipun mungkin ada pendekatan berbeda dalam penerapannya.

dprfendi: To be clear, Sri Mulyani never said that “teachers’ salaries are a burden on the state” to demean the teaching profession. What she explained in the state budget meeting was simply a fact: by law, 20% of the national budget must go to education, and around 60% of that portion is spent on salaries and allowances for teachers, lecturers, and school staff. That’s a matter of budget structure, not blaming teachers. She was also discussing how the remaining portion could be used for scholarships, training, research, and school facilities to improve the quality of education.
As for the clip where she said, “should everything come from the state budget, or should there be public participation,” that was from a forum at ITB discussing higher education funding — things like scholarships, alumni donations, or private sector partnerships (cost-sharing). It wasn’t about teachers’ salaries.
Cost-sharing isn’t some random idea she came up with. In developed countries like the U.S., the U.K., Germany, and Singapore, higher education is funded by a mix of government, students, private sector, and public donations — it’s a common practice. Just ask anyone who has studied or lived abroad.
That’s why people should check the primary sources and the context first, instead of getting worked up over news snippets. Media accounts thrive on traffic, and unfortunately, for the sake of clicks, some of them are willing to twist stories until they become misleading or even outright hoaxes.
